He is originally commissioned by Exchange crime lord Davik Kang to infiltrate the Sith military base as part of the plan to escape Sith martial law, but instead, he is bought by Revan at the suggestion of Canderous Ordo. T3-M4's skills are highly appreciated by Revan and he becomes a permanent crew member of the *Ebon Hawk*.

Assumption ends here.

## Development[]

*Star Wars: Knights of the Old Republic* was originally conceived around the [year](/wiki/Standard_year/Legends "Standard year/Legends") [2000](/wiki/2000 "2000") and was initially planned to be a game set around or during the Clone Wars, something like the storyline of [*Star Wars*: Episode II *Attack of the Clones*](/wiki/Star_Wars:_Episode_II_Attack_of_the_Clones "Star Wars: Episode II Attack of the Clones"), it was even supposed to have a subplot focusing on [clones](/wiki/Cloning/Legends "Cloning/Legends") but it was cut so it wouldn't spoil the then upcoming movie.[[11]](#cite_note-Blog-DrewK|5-11) BioWare was also given the option to set the game 4,000 years in the past and the company chose the latter as it would give them more creative freedom.[[12]](#cite_note-Article1-12) The team originally pitched the name ***Star Wars: Age of the Jedi*** to LucasArts, and even developed a logo with gold bars around the words in the style of the original movies. However, LucasArts rejected that title, as it was too close to [*Star Wars*: Episode VI *Return of the Jedi*](/wiki/Star_Wars:_Episode_VI_Return_of_the_Jedi "Star Wars: Episode VI Return of the Jedi"); BioWare's team was confused by this comparison, but a LucasArts representative suggested *Knights of the Old Republic* instead, and the name stuck.[[13]](#cite_note-BioWare-13)

From the beginning, the game was planned to have a cinematic feel, where you could see your character, and your party members at all times, like in the movies.[[12]](#cite_note-Article1-12) The process with [LucasArts](/wiki/LucasArts "LucasArts") was very smooth and only minor objections were made by the production giant, only about the way some things looked or how an event flowed with the plot. Having up to date lighting and the best graphics of its time made this game more incredible than the designers could have imagined.[[14]](#cite_note-Knight_fever-14)

When creating the planet of Taris, the game developers wanted to give the player an extended look at a world as an introduction. The decision to ravage the surface came with the need to provide the games's antagonist, Darth Malak, with a defining, establishing moment. They wanted to use the player's affinity for the world to make this action more poignant and a strong representation of just how evil Malak was.[[15]](#cite_note-Returning_to_Taris-15)

### Re-releases[]

:   "*We are very excited to be able to bring these classic interactive titles to our platform; it has been a long-time dream of ours. Luckily, Disney Interactive is always looking for new ways to give players access to content, so this was a natural partnership. To those gamers playing these titles for the first time…May the Force Be With You!*"
:   ―Guillaume Rambourg, GOG.com managing director[[16]](#cite_note-GOG.com_Announcement-16)

 [![Star Wars: Knights of the Old Republic GOG](data:image/gif;base64,R0lGODlhAQABAIABAAAAAP///yH5BAEAAAEALAAAAAABAAEAQAICTAEAOw%3D%3D)](https://static.wikia.nocookie.net/starwars/images/a/a4/KOTOR-GOG.png/revision/latest?cb=20141031062546) [![Star Wars: Knights of the Old Republic GOG](https://static.wikia.nocookie.net/starwars/images/a/a4/KOTOR-GOG.png/revision/latest/scale-to-width-down/300?cb=20141031062546)](https://static.wikia.nocookie.net/starwars/images/a/a4/KOTOR-GOG.png/revision/latest?cb=20141031062546) 

*Star Wars: Knights of the Old Republic* GOG.com re-release logo

 

*Knights of the Old Republic* has been made available several times since its initial release. The game was released on the online distribution service [Steam](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Steam_(service) "wikipedia:Steam (service)"),[[17]](#cite_note-Steam-17) along with its sequel *[Star Wars: Knights of the Old Republic II: The Sith Lords](/wiki/Star_Wars:_Knights_of_the_Old_Republic_II:_The_Sith_Lords "Star Wars: Knights of the Old Republic II: The Sith Lords")*. The game has also been released on iOS and Android systems by Aspyr Media and is available on the Apple App Store[[2]](#cite_note-KOTOR_iOS-2) and the Google Play Store.[[4]](#cite_note-KOTOR_android_app-4)

On [October 28](/wiki/October_28 "October 28"), [2014](/wiki/2014 "2014"), [Disney Interactive](/wiki/Disney_Interactive "Disney Interactive") announced a new partnership with GOG.com, a DRM-free digital distributor, that would allow for more than twenty classic Lucasfilm video game titles to be re-released digitally for modern computers, including [*Star Wars: X-Wing*](/wiki/Star_Wars:_X-Wing_(video_game) "Star Wars: X-Wing (video game)") and [*Star Wars: TIE Fighter*](/wiki/Star_Wars:_TIE_Fighter_(video_game) "Star Wars: TIE Fighter (video game)") and *Star Wars: Knights of the Old Republic*.[[16]](#cite_note-GOG.com_Announcement-16) In November of [2021](/wiki/2021 "2021"), the game was released on the [Nintendo Switch](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Nintendo_Switch "wikipedia:Nintendo Switch") system.[[5]](#cite_note-KOTOR_switch-5)

## Release and reception[]

:   "*Last Issue, the review for* Prince of Persia: The Forgotten Sands *incorrectly spelled the name* '*Malik*' *as* '*Malak.*' *A surprising number of readers noticed; we'll just hide behind the classic* '*We wish every game was* Knights of the Old Republic' *excuse.*"
:   ―*Game Informer* staff[[18]](#cite_note-Game_Informer_Mistake-18)

The general critical response was enthusiastic even before its release. After its unveiling at [E3](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/E3 "wikipedia:E3"), it won three Best Game at E3 awards in [2001](/wiki/2001 "2001") from [Womengamers](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Womengamers "wikipedia:Womengamers"), [GameSpot](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/GameSpot "wikipedia:GameSpot"), and [Voodoo Extreme](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Voodoo_Extreme "wikipedia:Voodoo Extreme") as well as ranking on [Next Gen Magazine's](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Next_Gen_Magazine "wikipedia:Next Gen Magazine") list.[[19]](#cite_note-Bioware_list_of_awards-19)

Since its release, *KotOR* has won one-hundred-twenty-six awards.[[19]](#cite_note-Bioware_list_of_awards-19) Forty-eight were various forms of Game of the Year Award, including [Game Developers Choice Awards'](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Game_Developers_Choice_Awards "wikipedia:Game Developers Choice Awards")' best game of the year,[[20]](#cite_note-GDCA-20) [BAFTA Games Awards](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/BAFTA_Games_Awards "wikipedia:BAFTA Games Awards")' best Xbox game,[[21]](#cite_note-BAFTA-21) and [IGN's](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/IGN "wikipedia:IGN") Best Overall Game of the year.[[22]](#cite_note-IGN_Award-22) IGN also ranked *KotOR* 3rd on its list of the best films and video games of the 2000-2009 decade.[[23]](#cite_note-IGN_decade_award-23) Furthermore, it has won thirty-three Best RPG Awards[[19]](#cite_note-Bioware_list_of_awards-19) such as the [Interactive Achievement Award](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Interactive_Achievement_Awards "wikipedia:Interactive Achievement Awards") for best console RPG and best computer RPG,[[24]](#cite_note-AIAS_Award-24) and GameSpot's Best Xbox Game of 2003[[25]](#cite_note-GameSpot_Award_1-25) and Best Role-Playing Game of 2003,[[26]](#cite_note-GameSpot_Award_2-26)

The game also won awards for its story and writing such as the Game Developers Choice Award for excellence in writing and for original character, HK-47,[[20]](#cite_note-GDCA-20) and an Interactive Achievement Award for best story/character development.[[24]](#cite_note-AIAS_Award-24) IGN gave it awards for Best Sound[[27]](#cite_note-IGN_Sound_Award-27) and Best Story,[[28]](#cite_note-IGN_Story_Award-28) and ranked it as the 27th Best Game of All Time.[[29]](#cite_note-IGN_Top_100-29) In 2007, the plot twist in *KotOR* was ranked number two in [Game Informer's](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Game_Informer "wikipedia:Game Informer") list of the top ten video game plot twists of all time[[30]](#cite_note-Game_Informer_168-30) and number 10 on [Screwattack's](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Screwattack "wikipedia:Screwattack") "Top 10 OMGWTF Moments".[[31]](#cite_note-Gametrailers_OMGWTF-31)

The game is also part of The Xbox Platinum Series/Classics for sales in excess of 1 million units.[[32]](#cite_note-32)

One of the criticisms of the game is that it can involve extensive back-tracking. That is, the player has to make frequent, time-consuming, in-game trips back to a previous locations along passages that have already been explored and cleared.[[33]](#cite_note-Game_Level_Design-33)

The soundtrack was composed by [Jeremy Soule](/wiki/Jeremy_Soule "Jeremy Soule")[[34]](#cite_note-34) for which he won [RPG Vault's](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/RPG_Vault "wikipedia:RPG Vault") Outstanding Achievement in Music Award, and [GameSpy's](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/GameSpy "wikipedia:GameSpy") Best Music: PC Award.[[19]](#cite_note-Bioware_list_of_awards-19)

The [Los Angeles Times](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Los_Angeles_Times "wikipedia:Los Angeles Times") listed *Knights of the Old Republic* as one of the most essential works of the *Star Wars* Expanded Universe.[[35]](#cite_note-LA_Times_Gallery-35)

When *Knights of the Old Republic* was ported to iPad in [2013](/wiki/2013 "2013") by [Aspyr Media](/wiki/Aspyr_Media "Aspyr Media"), there was renewed interest in the game, overwhelmingly positive. Multiple game review outlets still considered it one of the best *Star Wars* games ever made ten years later.[[36]](#cite_note-IGN2013-36)[[37]](#cite_note-Kotaku2013-37) The IGN reviewers were allowed early access to the app. They praised the port's handling of the touch interface on all counts, from combat to menu maneuvering, aside from movement, which required dragging a finger across the screen.[[36]](#cite_note-IGN2013-36)

*Star Wars: Knights of the Old Republic* receives "universal acclaim" reviews and was tagged as a "must-play" game on reviews aggregator Metacritic holding a metascore of 94/100 on Xbox,[[38]](#cite_note-Metacritic_Xbox-38) 93/100 on PC[[39]](#cite_note-Metacritic_PC-39) and 88/100 on iOS.[[40]](#cite_note-Metacritic_iOS-40)

## Continuity[]

Additionally, the game provided a full history of Tatooine and also explained the origins of Kashyyyk's ecosystem. It also offers up an alternate theory as to the original home planet of [Humans](/wiki/Human/Legends "Human/Legends") by having a Sand People historian remark on the player's similarity to the ancients of their people, kidnapped by the Rakata many years before, implying that Tatooine is in fact the planet on which Humans originated. In order to emphasize its place in continuity, there are references and future events (like a possible first contact with the [Yuuzhan Vong](/wiki/Yuuzhan_Vong "Yuuzhan Vong")).[[41]](#cite_note-41)

As the game is set during a period long before the familiar films, the creators modeled their 'universe' on many characters and details from the movies, as well as including mentions of conceptual ancestors (for example, the Sith fighter is considered to be an ancestor of the later [Sith Infiltrator](/wiki/Scimitar/Legends "Scimitar/Legends")) but not always (while [Sith troopers](/wiki/Sith_trooper_(Sith_Empire) "Sith trooper (Sith Empire)") seem to be based on the movie-era [stormtroopers](/wiki/Stormtrooper/Legends "Stormtrooper/Legends"), it doesn't mean the [clone troopers](/wiki/Clone_trooper/Legends "Clone trooper/Legends") were historically based on them). Other examples of this include the modeling of characters, such as Darth Malak, a towering Dark Lord of the Sith who speaks through a vocabulator due to an old injury, very similar to [Darth Vader](/wiki/Anakin_Skywalker/Legends "Anakin Skywalker/Legends"), and the inclusion of Wookiee and droid companions as part of the player's party. Additionally, many scenes have direct analogues in the films, such as the capture of the main character's freighter smuggling vessel, the *Ebon Hawk*, by tractor beam, just as the [*Millennium Falcon*](/wiki/Millennium_Falcon/Legends "Millennium Falcon/Legends") was captured by the [Death Star](/wiki/DS-1_Orbital_Battle_Station/Legends "DS-1 Orbital Battle Station/Legends"), followed by a prison break and loss of a character on board a vessel, which is very similar to the Death Star scene in the original film.[[14]](#cite_note-Knight_fever-14)

There are also errors in regard to previous events such as the formation of the Republic. Several characters refer to it as having been established 15,000 years prior,[[42]](#cite_note-42) as opposed to the canonical 21,000[[43]](#cite_note-NEC-43) (although facts in the load file does state the Republic as being more than 20,000 years old).

### Alternatives in gameplay[]

*Knights of the Old Republic* has the option to choose different paths at points in the story, such as the order of planets visited and whether Revan followed the light or dark side. Also depending on character alignment, some Force powers will cost more or less "Force points" if Revan corresponds or conflicts with each ones' individual alignment. Core abilities, however, do not change cost.[[10]](#cite_note-KOTOR-10)

Several party members can be killed off by Revan, depending on the actions in dialogue the player takes. For example, it is possible to kill Juhani in one of two ways: provoke her to attack during the mission to remove the taint from Dantooine's fields,[[44]](#cite_note-44) or kill her, this time alongside Jolee Bindo, later on in the game while on Lehon.[[45]](#cite_note-45) The deaths, or their suggestion in conversation, of party members often have significant influences in dialogue to follow with the remaining crew, and in the case of Mission Vao, as stated in the section directly below, can even lead to party members attacking Revan willingly.[[46]](#cite_note-Trick-46)

The encounters with Darth Bandon and Calo Nord can happen on different planets depending on the order selected by the player. Calo appears on the first planet where a Star Map is successfully found and Bandon appears on the third. Both will have different people accompany them for every planet.[[10]](#cite_note-KOTOR-10)

While the order in which the Star Map planets are visited can vary based on player preference, the numeric designations of the level modules[[47]](#cite_note-warplist-47) and cutscene video files[[48]](#cite_note-movielist-48) in the game itself are arranged in the order Tatooine–Kashyyyk–Manaan–Korriban. This order is also stated by Bastila Shan in a cutscene played during the *Leviathan* level,[[49]](#cite_note-m40ac-49) and is the preferred order listed in the officially licensed strategy guide.[[50]](#cite_note-prima-50)

#### Dark side endings[]

Because of the various paths the player can take, most importantly the choice of a male or female Revan, the dark side ending can vary from player to player.[[10]](#cite_note-KOTOR-10)

##### Male[]

Assuming the player has chosen a male Revan, he fights his way up to the roof of the Lehon temple and encounters Bastila, who has been corrupted and turned to the dark side by Malak. To prove her worth as Malak's apprentice, she engages Revan in a duel, though the latter manages to fight her off. Bastila sees his potential as a Sith and seduces him with talk of power, regaining his place as Dark Lord, and a pledge to be his lover (If the Bastila romance was completed). Tempted, Revan agrees, earning his Sith eyes and hair,[[51]](#cite_note-KOTOR_DSMRev-51) and to prove his loyalty, he slays Juhani (if she was spared earlier in the game) and Jolee.[[51]](#cite_note-KOTOR_DSMRev-51) They return to the *Ebon Hawk* and inform the rest of the party of what has happened and that they plan to usurp Malak's mantle. Torn by the news, Carth runs into the forest, unwilling to believe that Revan could have done such a thing; the droids are programmed to follow Revan, regardless of his alignment; Canderous is overjoyed to be able to fight alongside such a leader and warrior; and Zaalbar has sworn a lifedebt to him, granting Revan his loyalty for as long as he lives. Mission is shocked at the revelation of what has transpired and refuses to join the Sith in their conquest after seeing what happened to Taris. She refuses to believe that Revan would kill her in cold blood. Revan can either kill her himself, or use the [Jedi](/wiki/Jedi/Legends "Jedi/Legends") [mind trick](/wiki/Mind_trick/Legends "Mind trick/Legends") and the leverage of Zaalbar's lifedebt to persuade the Wookiee into doing the deed.[[46]](#cite_note-Trick-46) (It is also possible to kill Zaalbar as well if Revan takes him on the Star Forge after having him kill Mission,[[46]](#cite_note-Trick-46) if Revan fails to persuade him, or if Revan simply decides to kill Mission personally.)[[52]](#cite_note-52) Onboard the Ebon Hawk, Darth Revan and Bastila receive a transmission from Admiral Forn Dodonna and decide to use the attacking Republic fleet as a distraction to get close enough to the Star Forge to land in a hangar bay by promising to use Bastila's Battle Meditation to support them.[[53]](#cite_note-53) They successfully land the Ebon Hawk on the Star Forge and meet a Jedi strike team sent by the Republic. Dark Jedi attack the hangar and Revan assists them in fending off the attackers, after they are victorious Revan decides that they are no longer useful to him and he kills the Jedi as well.[[54]](#cite_note-54) Before proceeding to fight Darth Malak, Revan also has the chance to kill Bastila as well onboard the Star Forge.[[55]](#cite_note-55) Finally, after killing Darth Malak himself, a gathering on Rakata Prime takes place and Revan officially repossesses the title of Sith Lord.[[56]](#cite_note-56)

##### Female[]

The female version of the dark side ending is virtually the same as the male one, though Carth notices the dark change in Revan as the story progresses. He decides to confront her about her falling and promises to protect Revan from going down a path of self-destruction.[[57]](#cite_note-57)

After she gives in to Bastila's offer to join her in killing Malak, she would tell the group the same thing as the male Revan would, though Carth's reaction varies slightly, saying that she is not the woman he fell in love with (if the Carth romance was completed) before running away.[[58]](#cite_note-58) Uncaring, she still kills Mission and flies up to the Star Forge in the *Ebon Hawk*. After Revan kills Malak she heads back to the hangar to find Carth. Carth tells her that the Republic fleet picked him up from the planet surface and that he informed them of her betrayal. He also told them that he couldn't give up on her. He started to persuade her back to the light when Bastila entered the room and convinced Revan to stay on her current path. Revan kills Carth, and returns to Rakata Prime to retake her title as Sith Lord. In a cut-scene that did not make it to the final game, Revan had a third option to kill Bastila and die aboard the Star Forge with Carth. It was not placed in the final version because the developers did not have enough time for finishing the game. However, these features can be returned to the game through modding.[[59]](#cite_note-59)

#### Female light side ending[]

If Revan was specified as a woman, the player and Carth would start flirting on the surface of Taris right away,[[60]](#cite_note-KOTOR_Carth-60) though they would verbally fight later over Carth's trust issues. The story in the middle is the same until they reach Lehon. After Revan returns from the temple, Carth and Revan admit their feelings for each other.[[61]](#cite_note-61) Flying up to the Star Forge and fighting Malak goes exactly the same as the male version but Revan and Bastila don't profess their love for each other.[[62]](#cite_note-62)

A female Revan can also tease Carth throughout the story.[[60]](#cite_note-KOTOR_Carth-60) It can eventually get to the point where he wants to spank her to teach her a lesson.[[63]](#cite_note-63) If the Carth romance is not completed, Juhani may say that she loves Revan. Nothing else is said between them about it for the rest of the game.[[64]](#cite_note-64)

### Cut content[]

Cut content features the planet [Sleheyron](/wiki/Sleheyron/Legends "Sleheyron/Legends") and an alternate ending for a dark side female PC's romance with Carth, which the player could choose to kill Bastila and die on the Star Forge with Carth.[[65]](#cite_note-65)

In an attempt to truly complete the game, Team Hutt from Holowan Laboratories has been attempting to restore Sleheyron.[[66]](#cite_note-TeamHutt-66)

Several sequences were also cut out of Tatooine. One of them was that the Star Map was originally supposed to be located in the maw of a [Sarlacc](/wiki/Sarlacc/Legends "Sarlacc/Legends") pit and the character had to find a way to reach it without being eaten. Another was the character could become a messiah figure to the Sandpeople and would lead them against Czerka Corporation. There was also cut content relative to the planet Taris, cut mostly due to pacing issues rather than time constraints. Initially, there was to be another level to the Vulkar base there,[[67]](#cite_note-ACE_Q&A-67) containing a spice lab, staff housing, and the base's heating control system. The player had to retrieve the keycard that would access the garage elevator from a Vulkar who would trade said keycard in return for some spice. Another means of taking it from the gang member was by killing them. The level was accessed by an elevator that would have been the armory in the final version and was guarded by the same pair of droids. Also included on the cut level was a female pazaak playing member who was left with a male voiceover in the data left by Bioware.[[68]](#cite_note-Vulkar_Base_Restoration-68) The Gamorrean slavers were to have a base in the Undercity and there was going to be a [trash compactor](/wiki/Garbage_compactor/Legends "Garbage compactor/Legends") puzzle sequence in the sewers as well.[[67]](#cite_note-ACE_Q&A-67)

Additionally, there were two other confirmed sequences cut from the game. One takes place on Manaan if the player beats [Bendak Starkiller](/wiki/Gorse_Bendak "Gorse Bendak") in the dueling ring on Taris. [Deadeye Duncan](/wiki/Deadeye_Duncan "Deadeye Duncan") shows up in the docking area, telling how he escaped the destruction of Taris and asks if he can use the name [Mysterious Stranger](/wiki/Mysterious_Stranger "Mysterious Stranger").[[69]](#cite_note-69) The second takes place on Korriban: Bastila was originally intended to be allowed to accompany Revan to the Academy. If Revan provoked [Lashowe](/wiki/Lashowe "Lashowe") during their first meeting then Bastila would have interjected.[[70]](#cite_note-70)

Though not necessarily *cut* content, as it was left unsuppressed in the game files, Bastila was originally supposed to have a scene with [Nemo](/wiki/Nemo "Nemo"), an elderly Jedi from the enclave. They'd known each other for a long time and he asked her if she'd gotten her anger problems under control, revealing that her master used to dump [water](/wiki/Water/Legends "Water/Legends") over her head when she became frustrated. This scene is impossible to view outside of modding as when Bastila rejoins the party so they can go to the mysterious ruins, Nemo has already gone there ahead of them and died.

Some of this content, including the Deadeye Duncan encounter on Manaan, the alternate dark side ending, and the extra scene with Bastila can be restored in the form of community-created add-on modifications. These are only available for the PC version.[[71]](#cite_note-JdNoa-71)

### 2014 reboot[]

After the Expanded Universe was rebranded [*Star Wars* Legends](/wiki/Star_Wars_Legends "Star Wars Legends") in 2014, [Pablo Hidalgo](/wiki/Pablo_Hidalgo "Pablo Hidalgo") confirmed that many fans of *Knights of the Old Republic* worked at Lucasfilm, and concepts from the game have been used in *[Star Wars: The Clone Wars](/wiki/Star_Wars:_The_Clone_Wars "Star Wars: The Clone Wars")* or products released after the announcement. These include [Rakata Prime](/wiki/Rakata_Prime "Rakata Prime"), [Taris](/wiki/Taris "Taris"), [Malachor](/wiki/Malachor "Malachor"), [terentateks](/wiki/Terentatek "Terentatek"), [Manaan](/wiki/Manaan "Manaan") and the [selkaths](/wiki/Selkath "Selkath"), [*Sphyrna*-class Hammerhead corvette](/wiki/Sphyrna-class_Hammerhead_corvette "Sphyrna-class Hammerhead corvette"), and [pazaak](/wiki/Pazaak "Pazaak").[[72]](#cite_note-RebelsRecon-#2.12:_Inside_The_Protector_of_Concord_Dawn_|_Star_Wars_Rebels-72)

## Game mechanics ‡[]

*Star Wars: Knights of the Old Republic* is a role-playing game in the *Star Wars* universe and is set across different planets. The player's character and his party collect numerous items, armor, weapons, and learn many abilities along the way.

### Items[]

Many different objects can be found by Revan scattered all through the game world in different containers such as in [footlockers](/wiki/Footlocker/Legends "Footlocker/Legends"), baskets, and corpses. What items can be taken from the containers are determined through random drops unless said item is required for story progression. Items can also be bought or sold in shops spread through the game through an exchange of credits, the game's monetary unit.

All items are organized in an inventory which can be reached in the start menu at any point outside of a conversation. It has the ability to filter in a specific type of item, such as weapons, so that only that kind of item is shown. It is organized into all items, utility items, usable items, equippable items, quest items, and new items, which are marked by a purple coloring. Utility items include [stimulants](/wiki/Stimulant/Legends "Stimulant/Legends") which raise stats for a short amount of time, medical items such as [medpacs](/wiki/Medpac/Legends "Medpac/Legends") or [antidote kits](/wiki/Antidote_kit "Antidote kit") used for regaining health or fixing status effects, multiple types of [grenade](/wiki/Grenade/Legends "Grenade/Legends") that cause different damage types or status effects, many kinds of armable [mines](/wiki/Mine/Legends "Mine/Legends"), armor, weapon, and lightsaber upgrades such as different [crystals](/wiki/Lightsaber_crystal/Legends "Lightsaber crystal/Legends"); as well as spikes for hacking [computers](/wiki/Computer_spike/Legends "Computer spike/Legends") or bypassing [security](/wiki/Security_spike "Security spike"). Quest items include items required for advancing the story, such as the Star Map data, or for completing many side-quests, such as datapads. Useable items also include medical items, stimulants, and equippable personal shields.

Droids used different sets of items for healing and equipment, aside from weapons.

#### Equippable items[]

Equippable items are collected throughout the game and are used to enhance the party. There are nine equipment slots per character: headgear, [implants](/wiki/Cybernetics/Legends "Cybernetics/Legends"), armor, gloves, personal shields, right and left shoulders; a belt, and weapons; right and left hands. Headgear includes anything worn upon the character's head, such as a [helmet](/wiki/Armor/Legends "Armor/Legends") or [visor](/wiki/Davik%27s_Visor "Davik's Visor"), and normally are used for either protection or sensory enhancement. Implants are placed in the character's body to enhance certain statistics and sometimes grant Feats or Skills. Armor is worn on the body for protection and for modesty. Personal shields are worn upon a character's shoulders and they create a protective force around a person in order to protect that person from damage for a limited time. Belts are worm around the character's waist and increase certain stats. Weapons are tools the character can use to kill enemies both organic and droid. They are carried with the character's hands and increase damage dealt by the character. Unarmed combat is also possible and skill with this style of fighting increases as the character gains levels.

#### Weapons[]

Weapons are items found throughout the game world, primarily in shops or in lockers. They can be equipped to each character individually, held in the hand equip slots, and add to the amount of damage points a character can deal to opponents. Generally, one weapon can be placed in each hand but some, such as [blaster rifles](/wiki/Blaster_rifle/Legends "Blaster rifle/Legends") or [bowcasters](/wiki/Bowcaster/Legends "Bowcaster/Legends"), must be held with both hands, forfeiting the second slot. The player can decide which weapon is in the character's dominant hand, which will never receive penalties in combat, while the other becomes the off-hand and will receive damage and accuracy deductions because of it. These penalties can be offset by certain advanced Feats or Skills as well as using a [short blade](/wiki/Short_sword "Short sword") in this hand. Certain weapons require specific Feats and Skills to be learned before they can be used.

There are two forms of weapons found in *Knights of the Old Republic*, [melee](/wiki/Melee/Legends "Melee/Legends"), generally [swords](/wiki/Sword/Legends "Sword/Legends"), and ranged, blasters. Each has different strengths, weaknesses, damage types, and upgrades. Weapons can be upgraded using workbenches and different parts gathered by the player.

Melee weapons are used to assist hand-to-hand combatants at short range. These include various swords, [staves](/wiki/Quarterstaff/Legends "Quarterstaff/Legends"), [vibroweapons](/wiki/Vibro-weapon/Legends "Vibro-weapon/Legends"), [axes](/wiki/Axe/Legends "Axe/Legends"), and lightsabers. These weapons cannot be used at a distance but have great effect against unarmed opponents or those carrying blasters. However, because of their limited range, a character using a melee weapon is vulnerable to an enemy using a blaster at a distance and must first close that distance before they can attack. Certain swords and other melee weapons can be enhanced by using a workbench to add parts collected throughout the game. There are three specific parts that can be added to enhance applicable standard melee weapons. Lightsabers are another form of melee weapon that can only be used by a Jedi. They come in various colors and with various damage types, depending on different lightsaber crystals inserted in three crystal chambers.

Ranged weapons are all the various blasters and other guns the player can use. They are used primarily from long range, many combatants preferring to switch to swords when pressed into close quarters combat. They use another set of upgrade items, different from melee weapons, including a [hair trigger](/wiki/Hair_trigger/Legends "Hair trigger/Legends") and [scope](/wiki/Scope/Legends "Scope/Legends") which increase the weapon's accuracy or damage.

### Levels[]

A Level is a number used to define the strength of a character. As a character gains Levels, by accumulating experience, they earn points which are spent on augmenting the character's Attributes and Skills. They are also given the opportunity to learn new Feats and Force-sensitives have access to the discovery new Force powers.

Experience, abbreviated XP, is accumulated by completing various quests and defeating enemies. After reaching a certain number, which rises with each level, the character will "Level Up" and be given the chance to allot the new points to the attribute fields. Equal experience is given to all party members, regardless of whether the character was in the three-man squad used on the planet or not. Revan begins the journey at Level 1 and after he character surpasses Level 6, new characters are brought into the party at Level 6 with all experience gained through the journey shared with them.

#### Skills[]

In all there are eight Skills, each corresponding to an Attribute.

* Computer Use, related to Intelligence, is used to calculate the chances a character will be able to slice a computer to perform a variety of situational tasks, such as disable a gun turret or open a magnetically sealed door. These tasks require the use of computer spikes, though the number needed is decreased by one for every four points put into this skill.
* Demolitions, also related to Intelligence, is used to set, disable, or destroy mines around the game world. At least one point must be put into this skill to be able to access any actions relative to mines or to use grenades. Mines come in a variety of types, though there are three difficulties: easy, medium, and high difficulties; each requiring better rolls to complete, though a very bad roll can result in a mine's premature explosion.
* Stealth, related to Dexterity, is required to use the [stealth field generator](/wiki/Stealth_field_generator/Legends "Stealth field generator/Legends") items and entering Stealth Mode. While in Stealth Mode, the character is put into Solo Mode and is undetectable, if the enemies Awareness stats are beaten by the character's Stealth stat, even if they are in the enemy's direct line of sight. While in Stealth Mode, a character must walk slowly unless they have learned the Stealth Run Feat, other than that, they will be able to perform all tasks except communication or combat. These disrupt the field and eject the character from Stealth Mode.
* Awareness, related to Wisdom, is used to determine if a character notices mines or enemies using stealth technology. It is always active, though there is a penalty to its effectiveness if the character is running.
* Persuade, related to Charisma, is a skill that only Revan can learn. It determines whether or not the player can convince an NPC of something. The option only appears in conversation when there is something a character is hiding or knows that could help the character in a quest. It can also be used to convince them to do something. Certain requests can be harder to convince a character to do: asking a guard to lift a [bounty](/wiki/Bounty/Legends "Bounty/Legends") on someone's head would be easier than asking the same guard to leave his post.
* Repair corresponds with Intelligence, it allows the character to perform repairs on machines and droids with the use of Parts. The more complicated the repair, the more Parts are needed but for every four points put into this Skill, the total number required is decreased by one. This skill also increases the total number of Vitality Points that are recovered when using a repair kit on T3 or HK.
* Security is the final skill related to Intelligence and it is used to access electronic locking devices. It is used to deactivate locks on door and storage containers. The Skill can be augmented by using security spikes and [tunnelers](/wiki/Security_spike_tunneler "Security spike tunneler"), the more advanced of the two. At least one point must be invested for this skill to be usable by a character and as an alternative, a character may use its current weapon to bash doors down or open crates.
* Treat Injury is related to Wisdom. The more points invested in this skill, the more vitality points are regained when the character uses a medpac on itself or another character. Advanced medpacs and life support packs further amplify this Skill during their use.

### Character alignment[]

The player's Force attunement is determined by actions taken through the game, mostly through conversation. As the player talks to the many NPCs through the game worlds, he will be confronted with moral dilemmas and it is up to the player to decide how he should respond. While talking to the characters, the player is given options for him to say, some that lean towards the light side of the Force, others that lean to the dark, and some more neutral responses that lead to no shifts. These decisions, when they lead to an alignment shift, culminate in accumulating light side or dark side "points" which are used to determine how far the character leans to one side.

As the player leans more to the dark side, his appearance begins to change, relative to the character model chosen at the beginning of the game. Generally, he becomes pale and his hair color starts to fade. When player leans completely to one side, he earns "Mastery" of that side and surges with the Force, earning a bonus in battle.

### Classes[]

Upon starting a new game, the player is given a choice between three different classes for the player character: [Scout](/wiki/Scout/Legends "Scout/Legends"), [Scoundrel](/wiki/Scoundrel/Legends "Scoundrel/Legends"), and Soldier. Each has the player character's abilities develop in a different way, accentuating different styles of play, and grant different starting abilities. After the player character is taken to Dantooine, he becomes a Jedi Padawan. At this point, the player is given another choice between three classes. These in turn alter the way the player character's Force powers develop. The three classes are [Jedi Consular](/wiki/Jedi_Consular "Jedi Consular"), Jedi Sentinel, and [Jedi Guardian](/wiki/Jedi_Guardian/Legends "Jedi Guardian/Legends").

## Legacy[]

### *Star Wars: Knights of the Old Republic II: The Sith Lords*[]

:   "*The call of* The Sith Lords *is impossible to resist.*"
:   ―Joe Juba, in his review of *Knigts of the Old Republic 2*[[73]](#cite_note-Juba_quote-73)

 [![Star Wars: Knights of the Old Republic II box art.](data:image/gif;base64,R0lGODlhAQABAIABAAAAAP///yH5BAEAAAEALAAAAAABAAEAQAICTAEAOw%3D%3D)](https://static.wikia.nocookie.net/starwars/images/d/d9/Kotoriibox.jpg/revision/latest?cb=20060603062220) [![Star Wars: Knights of the Old Republic II box art.](https://static.wikia.nocookie.net/starwars/images/d/d9/Kotoriibox.jpg/revision/latest/scale-to-width-down/200?cb=20060603062220)](https://static.wikia.nocookie.net/starwars/images/d/d9/Kotoriibox.jpg/revision/latest?cb=20060603062220) 

*Star Wars: Knights of the Old Republic II* box art.

 

*Star Wars: Knights of the Old Republic II: The Sith Lords* was developed by a different studio, [Obsidian Entertainment](/wiki/Obsidian_Entertainment "Obsidian Entertainment"),[[74]](#cite_note-Tech_info-74) using an improved version of the engine from the first game. Development for this game began about the same time the first game released, [July 15](/wiki/July_15 "July 15"), [2003](/wiki/2003 "2003"). It was released for Xbox in [December](/wiki/December "December") [2004](/wiki/2004 "2004") and PC on [February 8](/wiki/February_8 "February 8") [2005](/wiki/2005 "2005").[[74]](#cite_note-Tech_info-74) Dubbed "KotOR 2" by fans, the game takes place five years after the events of the original.[[9]](#cite_note-TEA-9) From the onset, the tone of the galaxy was set to be much more dark than the first game and the state of affairs for the Jedi Order was to be bleak.[[75]](#cite_note-GameSpot_Interview-75)

The game introduces a new protagonist, the [Jedi Exile](/wiki/Meetra_Surik "Meetra Surik"), on a mission to reunite the members of the [Jedi High Council](/wiki/Jedi_High_Council/Legends "Jedi High Council/Legends") following the Jedi Order's virtual [elimination](/wiki/First_Jedi_Purge "First Jedi Purge") at the hands of two Sith Lords, Darths [Sion](/wiki/Darth_Sion "Darth Sion") and [Nihilus](/wiki/Darth_Nihilus "Darth Nihilus")[[76]](#cite_note-K2-76) and game features a brand new party, with HK-47, T3-M4, and Canderous Ordo, now using his new title as [Mandalore](/wiki/Mandalore_(title)/Legends "Mandalore (title)/Legends"), returning. The Exile travels to six new worlds as well as two planets, Dantooine and Korriban, that were part of the original game. The *Ebon Hawk* also returns as the player's primary form of transportation.[[76]](#cite_note-K2-76)

The game also added hundreds of new weapons and characters to *Star Wars* canon. It referenced *Tales of the Jedi* as well as other works from the [Old Republic era](/wiki/Old_Republic_era "Old Republic era") and even events such as the fall of the Galactic Republic in [19 BBY](/wiki/19_BBY/Legends "19 BBY/Legends"). Many characters' personal effects, such as [Thon](/wiki/Thon "Thon")'s [Robe](/wiki/Thon%27s_Robe "Thon's Robe") and [Ludo Kressh](/wiki/Ludo_Kressh "Ludo Kressh")'s [War Sword](/wiki/Ludo_Kressh%27s_War_Sword "Ludo Kressh's War Sword"), could be found by the Exile as random drops. Some characters from the first game reappeared in roles of varying importance. Vrook Lamar makes a reappearance as one of the Jedi Masters that the Exile seeks out during her journey. Revan and Malak both make reappearances as visions to the Exile in the [Tomb of Ludo Kressh](/wiki/Tomb_of_Ludo_Kressh "Tomb of Ludo Kressh") and both characters are defeated by the Exile. Bastila Shan and Carth Onasi, both major players in the Republic, return in minor roles.[[76]](#cite_note-K2-76)

The sequel introduced a brand new "Influence" system, which is not unlike the way both games calculate dark side/light side shifts. It keeps track of what your party members feel about your responses to certain situations or how you talk to them in conversation. By gaining amounts of "Influence" with a certain character, through player actions or choice of conversational topics, they may reveal more about themselves or allow you to instruct them in the ways of the Force so they can re-class as Jedi. Depending on the "Influence" level you have with a party member, that party member will be either drawn closer to or further from your alignment, unlike the first game. Many of the characters in your party will have different appearances based on their alignments, just as the player's character does.[[76]](#cite_note-K2-76)

Another new game mechanic introduced is the prestige class. After a certain point in the game, the Exile may choose one of three classes. If the Exile follows the light side of the Force, the [Jedi Watchman](/wiki/Jedi_Watchman/Legends "Jedi Watchman/Legends"), the Jedi Master, or the [Jedi Weapon Master](/wiki/Jedi_Weapon_Master "Jedi Weapon Master") classes are available. Alternatively, if the Exile chooses to follow the dark side, the choices are changed to a counterpart of the Light Side classes, namely the [Sith assassin](/wiki/Sith_assassin/Legends "Sith assassin/Legends"), Sith Lord, and [Sith Marauder](/wiki/Sith_Marauder "Sith Marauder") respectively. If the Exile shifts her Force alignment after choosing a prestige class, the class automatically changes to reflect that by becoming its counterpart.[[76]](#cite_note-K2-76)

### *Star Wars: Knights of the Old Republic* comics series[]

:   "*It's all Star Wars, whenever it takes place.*"
:   ―[John Jackson Miller](/wiki/John_Jackson_Miller "John Jackson Miller")[[77]](#cite_note-JMM_quote-77)

 [![The first issue of the comics series](data:image/gif;base64,R0lGODlhAQABAIABAAAAAP///yH5BAEAAAEALAAAAAABAAEAQAICTAEAOw%3D%3D)](https://static.wikia.nocookie.net/starwars/images/7/7e/Swkotor1cover.jpg/revision/latest?cb=20131017022632) [![The first issue of the comics series](https://static.wikia.nocookie.net/starwars/images/7/7e/Swkotor1cover.jpg/revision/latest/scale-to-width-down/200?cb=20131017022632)](https://static.wikia.nocookie.net/starwars/images/7/7e/Swkotor1cover.jpg/revision/latest?cb=20131017022632) 

The first issue of the comics series

 

On [January 25](/wiki/January_25 "January 25"), [2006](/wiki/2006 "2006") the first issue of the [comic book](/wiki/Star_Wars_comic_books "Star Wars comic books") series [*Star Wars: Knights of the Old Republic*](/wiki/Star_Wars:_Knights_of_the_Old_Republic_(comic_series) "Star Wars: Knights of the Old Republic (comic series)") was printed. The series was created to serve as a sequel to *Tales of the Jedi* and a prequel to *Knights of the Old Republic* began production with [Dark Horse Comics](/wiki/Dark_Horse_Comics "Dark Horse Comics"). First announced in [July](/wiki/July "July") of the previous year at Comic-Con, the series would take place between [3964](/wiki/3964_BBY "3964 BBY") and [3963 BBY](/wiki/3963_BBY "3963 BBY"), detailing the life of a brand new protagonist named [Zayne Carrick](/wiki/Zayne_Carrick "Zayne Carrick"), a Padawan framed for the [murder of his fellow students](/wiki/Padawan_Massacre "Padawan Massacre") at the [Jedi Tower](/wiki/Jedi_Tower "Jedi Tower") training academy on Taris. The comics also coincided with the run up to and outbreak of the Mandalorian Wars, a conflict heavily referenced in both the original *Knights of the Old Republic*. The series ended with [Demon, Part 4](/wiki/Knights_of_the_Old_Republic_50 "Knights of the Old Republic 50"), the 50th issue, released on [February 17](/wiki/February_17 "February 17"), [2010](/wiki/2010 "2010").[[78]](#cite_note-DarkHorseWebsite-78)

#### Game characters[]

Many characters from *Knights of the Old Republic* cross paths with Carrick.[[79]](#cite_note-K8-79)[[80]](#cite_note-K30-80) They take many roles throughout, from major galactic players[[81]](#cite_note-K42-81) to one-off characters and some befriend him.[[82]](#cite_note-K22-82)[[83]](#cite_note-K31-83)

Carth Onasi, first as a [helmsman](/wiki/Helm_officer/Legends "Helm officer/Legends") aboard the Republic ship, [*Courageous*](/wiki/Courageous_(Inexpugnable-class) "Courageous (Inexpugnable-class)"), in [Issue 8](/wiki/Knights_of_the_Old_Republic_8 "Knights of the Old Republic 8"), and later as a [Lieutenant](/wiki/Lieutenant/Legends "Lieutenant/Legends") in his next appearance, [Issue 14](/wiki/Knights_of_the_Old_Republic_14 "Knights of the Old Republic 14") onwards. In [Issue 31](/wiki/Knights_of_the_Old_Republic_31 "Knights of the Old Republic 31") he was removed from his bridge post for "losing" Carrick after fighting alongside the Jedi and developing a friendship with him. He was reassigned to a squadron of [Aurek-class strikefighters](/wiki/Aurek-class_tactical_strikefighter "Aurek-class tactical strikefighter"), Onasi allowed Carrick to escape from him yet again, this time from an engagement between the Aurek squadron and the starship *[Moomo Williwaw](/wiki/Moomo_Williwaw "Moomo Williwaw")*. Carrick slinked away in the junkhauler *[Deadweight](/wiki/Deadweight "Deadweight")*. In the [penultimate issue](/wiki/Knights_of_the_Old_Republic_49 "Knights of the Old Republic 49"), Onasi was given back his post, on the bridge of the [*Inexpugnable*-class](/wiki/Inexpugnable-class_tactical_command_ship "Inexpugnable-class tactical command ship") [*Swiftsure*](/wiki/Swiftsure_(Inexpugnable-class) "Swiftsure (Inexpugnable-class)"), and fought to [capture](/wiki/Incident_near_Ithor_system "Incident near Ithor system") a [slaver](/wiki/The_Crucible "The Crucible") ship called the [*Gladiator*](/wiki/Gladiator_(Crucible) "Gladiator (Crucible)").

Saul Karath made an appearance, still an officer with the Galactic Republic as the story takes place before the Bombing of Telos IV, he first appears in Issue 8 aboard the *Courageous*, he presided over the Republic forces during several battles of the series, earning the rank of [Rear Admiral](/wiki/Rear_Admiral/Legends "Rear Admiral/Legends"). Later, before [Issue 30](/wiki/Knights_of_the_Old_Republic_30 "Knights of the Old Republic 30"), he was given command of the *Swiftsure*, ending a [Sith Acolyte's](/wiki/Haazen "Haazen") [rebellion](/wiki/Vindication "Vindication") against the Jedi Order. Karath bombarded the [estate](/wiki/Draay_Estate "Draay Estate") of Jedi Master [Lucien Draay](/wiki/Lucien_Draay "Lucien Draay"), where the Acolyte was hiding. The bombing killed many and was officially blamed on the Mandalorians, with Karath publicly prociaming his everlasting vengence on the accused. This incident would cast Karath as a hero in the minds of the Republic's citizens. He last appeared in Issue 49, commanding the *Swiftsure* when it captured the *Gladiator*. After that Zayne Carrick, who had anonymously informed Karath of the *Gladiator*'s presence, asked for passage to the planet [Osadia](/wiki/Osadia "Osadia"). Though Karath initially refused, Carrick threatened to reveal the truth of the bombing of Draay's estate, which prompted the Admiral to order the *Hammerhead*-class *[Testament](/wiki/Testament "Testament")* to take the former Padawan to his destination.

Mission Vao, then a five year old, met Carrick in the streets of Taris and became fast friends with him; going so far as to bite the leg of the then-Hidden Bek Brejik to protect the Jedi, though she was quickly pulled away by her brother Griff. Though Griff and Mission only appeared in [Issue 22](/wiki/Knights_of_the_Old_Republic_22 "Knights of the Old Republic 22"), Brejik, with Zaerdra, appeared both in 22 and [Issue 23](/wiki/Knights_of_the_Old_Republic_23 "Knights of the Old Republic 23"). Gadon Thek appears, still with his sight, in every issue of the [Knights of Suffering arc](/wiki/Star_Wars:_Knights_of_the_Old_Republic:_Knights_of_Suffering "Star Wars: Knights of the Old Republic: Knights of Suffering") spanning from Issue 22 to [Issue 24](/wiki/Knights_of_the_Old_Republic_24 "Knights of the Old Republic 24").

The Jedi Enclave Council makes an appearance early in the series, Issues [2](/wiki/Knights_of_the_Old_Republic_2 "Knights of the Old Republic 2") (a flashback), [4](/wiki/Knights_of_the_Old_Republic_4 "Knights of the Old Republic 4"), and [6](/wiki/Knights_of_the_Old_Republic_6 "Knights of the Old Republic 6") though its members appear in other parts of the series as well. Zhar Lestin appears only in Issues 4 and 6; Vrook Lamar appears in 4, 5, and 6, last appearing in [Issue 33](/wiki/Knights_of_the_Old_Republic_33 "Knights of the Old Republic 33") leading the assault on the Draay Estate before being forced back due to Karath's orbital bombardment. Vandar Tokare also appears in Issues 2, 4, 6, [9](/wiki/Knights_of_the_Old_Republic_9 "Knights of the Old Republic 9") (in a hologram), [12](/wiki/Knights_of_the_Old_Republic_12 "Knights of the Old Republic 12"), [29](/wiki/Knights_of_the_Old_Republic_29 "Knights of the Old Republic 29"), and last appeared in Issue 31, hearing Jedi Master [Xamar](/wiki/Xamar "Xamar") confess to being part of the cabal known as the [Jedi Covenant](/wiki/Jedi_Covenant "Jedi Covenant"). [Dorak](/wiki/Dorak "Dorak"), who appeared in the game as a member, was not yet on the council.

Revan himself appeared in the series, still a Jedi Knight at the time, but his face was always shrouded.[[84]](#cite_note-K0-84) The [prequel issue](/wiki/Knights_of_the_Old_Republic_0 "Knights of the Old Republic 0") marked his first of four showings, though he would be heavily referenced as the series progressed. He was known as "the Revanchist" as the leader of a [faction](/wiki/Revanchist "Revanchist") of Jedi who followed him to battle during the Mandalorian Wars.[[85]](#cite_note-K40-85) [Issue 42](/wiki/Knights_of_the_Old_Republic_42 "Knights of the Old Republic 42") revealed how Revan took up his name. On the planet Cathar a [dozen years](/wiki/3973_BBY "3973 BBY") before the events of the comics, Revan and the original Revanchists went to Cather searching for proof of the Mandalorian atrocities. There, he found the mask of a Mandalorian interred in the sand, which triggered a vision of the [Battle of Cathar](/wiki/Battle_of_Cathar "Battle of Cathar") for all present. The group witnessed a group of Cathar running from a band of Mandalorians when [one of the attackers](/wiki/Unidentified_Mandalorian_female "Unidentified Mandalorian female") pleaded for her commander to stop the attack as they'd already taken the world. Her words were unheeded, and she was killed alongside the Cathar; who were virtually rendered extinct. Revan put on the mask, which he would later wear as the Dark Lord, and swore to keep it on until the Mandalorians were wholly defeated. Issue 42 was also his final appearance.

The future Darth Malak, then known by his birth name of Alek Squinquargesimus,[[86]](#cite_note-K10-86) was depicted as Revan's loyal friend and a devout Revanchist. Alek was featured even more extensively than his "Master,"[[87]](#cite_note-K15-87) garnering appearances in 15 separate issues, giving context for several of his features in the game. For example, in Issue 29, an arrest warrant was placed on members of the Revanchists and when Malak was involved in a plan crafted by Zayne Carrick in Issue 31, he got his trademark blue tattoos before taking up the moniker "Captain Malak" as a disguise to avoid capture. The comics serial also revealed that Malak fell in love with an [Arkanian Offshoot](/wiki/Arkanian_Offshoot/Legends "Arkanian Offshoot/Legends") woman named [Jarael](/wiki/Jarael "Jarael"), who did not feel the same for him.[[88]](#cite_note-K23-88) On a few occasions, he offered her a place among the Revanchist ranks,[[81]](#cite_note-K42-81) though when Carrick kissed her in Issue 42, claiming they were together, he abandoned his ambitions.

[Cassus Fett](/wiki/Cassus_Fett "Cassus Fett"), a Mandalorian whose [weapon](/wiki/Cassus_Fett%27s_heavy_blaster_pistol "Cassus Fett's heavy blaster pistol") and [armor](/wiki/Cassus_Fett%27s_Battle_Armor "Cassus Fett's Battle Armor") can be found in the first *Knights of the Old Republic* game, appears extensively in the comics series as a [high ranking](/wiki/Field_Marshal/Legends "Field Marshal/Legends") Mandalorian soldier who is second only to [Mandalore the Ultimate](/wiki/Mandalore_the_Ultimate "Mandalore the Ultimate"),[[89]](#cite_note-The_Taris_Holofeed_Special_Proclamation-89) another individual mentioned in the game. Fett first appeared in Issue 8 and would appear in Issues 23, [27](/wiki/Knights_of_the_Old_Republic_27 "Knights of the Old Republic 27"), 42 (in a flashback), and 49. The Mandalore appeared in Issues 8, 20, and 21. A [*Dynamic*-class freighter](/wiki/Dynamic-class_freighter/Legends "Dynamic-class freighter/Legends") also makes an appearance in a tactical hologram that Fett used to monitor a [battle](/wiki/Taris_Siege "Taris Siege") taking place in Issue 23.

### *Star Wars: Knights of the Old Republic 3*[]

 [![Concept art of ](data:image/gif;base64,R0lGODlhAQABAIABAAAAAP///yH5BAEAAAEALAAAAAABAAEAQAICTAEAOw%3D%3D)](https://static.wikia.nocookie.net/starwars/images/8/8c/Naresha.jpg/revision/latest?cb=20090613104530) [![Concept art of ](https://static.wikia.nocookie.net/starwars/images/8/8c/Naresha.jpg/revision/latest/scale-to-width-down/150?cb=20090613104530)](https://static.wikia.nocookie.net/starwars/images/8/8c/Naresha.jpg/revision/latest?cb=20090613104530) 

Concept art of [Naresha](/wiki/Naresha "Naresha")

 

Another sequel, entitled *[Star Wars: Knights of the Old Republic 3](/wiki/Star_Wars:_Knights_of_the_Old_Republic_3 "Star Wars: Knights of the Old Republic 3")*, was put into extensive preproduction around [2004](/wiki/2004 "2004"), but the game was canceled when LucasArts hit an economic rough patch.[[90]](#cite_note-Rogue_Leaders:_The_Story_of_LucasArts-90) *[Rogue Leaders: The Story of LucasArts](/wiki/Rogue_Leaders:_The_Story_of_LucasArts "Rogue Leaders: The Story of LucasArts")*, a [2008](/wiki/2008 "2008") reference book by [Rob Smith](/wiki/Rob_Smith "Rob Smith") covering the history of LucasArts, first confirmed the pre-production of this sequel. Some planets were also confirmed to have been planned to make appearances in the game: [Coruscant](/wiki/Coruscant/Legends "Coruscant/Legends"); [Mandalore](/wiki/Mandalore/Legends "Mandalore/Legends") with a location known as [Mandalore City](/wiki/Mandalore_City "Mandalore City"); [Rodia](/wiki/Rodia/Legends "Rodia/Legends"); and [Taloraan](/wiki/Taloraan/Legends "Taloraan/Legends"). However, no plot details were released except that one of the characters in the game, with accompanying artwork, was a [female](/wiki/Gender/Legends "Gender/Legends") named "[Naresha](/wiki/Naresha "Naresha")." As the game was cancelled, its planned original elements, such as Naresha and Mandalore City, are considered non-canon as all other elements that were confirmed by the book had appeared in other *Star Wars* works.

After the second game was completed, Obsidian Entertainment expressed desires to make another sequel, as did LucasArts. However, no plans of making another *Knights of the Old Republic* game have come to fruition although representatives from LucasArts have said that they would not abandon the "franchise."[[91]](#cite_note-Continue-91)

### *Star Wars: The Old Republic*[]

:   ![Blue Glass Arrow](data:image/gif;base64,R0lGODlhAQABAIABAAAAAP///yH5BAEAAAEALAAAAAABAAEAQAICTAEAOw%3D%3D) *See also: [Star Wars: The Old Republic](/wiki/Star_Wars:_The_Old_Republic "Star Wars: The Old Republic")*

 [![Promo art of Star Wars: The Old Republic](data:image/gif;base64,R0lGODlhAQABAIABAAAAAP///yH5BAEAAAEALAAAAAABAAEAQAICTAEAOw%3D%3D)](https://static.wikia.nocookie.net/starwars/images/f/fb/Star_Wars_The_Old_Republic_Anniversary_Promo.jpg/revision/latest?cb=20200526154451) [![Promo art of Star Wars: The Old Republic](https://static.wikia.nocookie.net/starwars/images/f/fb/Star_Wars_The_Old_Republic_Anniversary_Promo.jpg/revision/latest/scale-to-width-down/250?cb=20200526154451)](https://static.wikia.nocookie.net/starwars/images/f/fb/Star_Wars_The_Old_Republic_Anniversary_Promo.jpg/revision/latest?cb=20200526154451) 

Promo art of Star Wars: The Old Republic

 

Formerly projected for a Spring 2011 release, BioWare began development on *[Star Wars: The Old Republic](/wiki/Star_Wars:_The_Old_Republic "Star Wars: The Old Republic")* in December 2005[[92]](#cite_note-KotOR_MMO_evidence-92) at a satellite studio in [Austin](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Austin,_Texas "wikipedia:Austin, Texas"), [Texas](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Texas "wikipedia:Texas") constructed primarily for the project.[[93]](#cite_note-BioWare_Austin-93)[[94]](#cite_note-E3_2008-94) In the following months, rumors persisted about the development of a new *Knights of the Old Republic* video game, spurred on by leaks from within BioWare[[95]](#cite_note-BioWare_Upcoming_MMO-95) and LucasArts[[96]](#cite_note-BioWare_MMO_Kotor3-96) and the registration of "Star Wars The Old Republic"[[97]](#cite_note-trademark1-97) and "The Old Republic"[[98]](#cite_note-trademark2-98) as LucasArts trademarks, before being officially announced at an invitation-only event for the press on [October 21](/wiki/October_21 "October 21"). During the E3 2008 expo, Electronic Arts executive John Riccitello confirmed that the MMO would be connected to the *[Knights of the Old Republic](/wiki/Knights_of_the_Old_Republic "Knights of the Old Republic")* series of video games.[[99]](#cite_note-EACEOconfirm-99) During the event, the official press release was finally published.[[100]](#cite_note-LucasArts-LucasArts_and_BioWare_reveal_Star_Wars:_The_Old_Republic-100) A trailer, titled "[Deceived](/wiki/Deceived "Deceived")," was released on [June 1](/wiki/June_1 "June 1"), 2009 at [E3](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Electronic_Entertainment_Expo "wikipedia:Electronic Entertainment Expo") [2009](/wiki/2009 "2009"). It depicted the [Sacking of Coruscant](/wiki/Sacking_of_Coruscant "Sacking of Coruscant"), narrated by a Sith Lord named [Darth Malgus](/wiki/Darth_Malgus "Darth Malgus").[[101]](#cite_note-Deceived-101) Another, entitled "[Hope](/wiki/Hope_(cinematic_trailer) "Hope (cinematic trailer)")" was released at E3 2010 and featured the [Battle of Alderaan](/wiki/Battle_of_Alderaan "Battle of Alderaan").[[102]](#cite_note-Hope-102)

Dark Horse Comics released an online-only comic book series entitled *[Star Wars: The Old Republic, Threat of Peace](/wiki/Star_Wars:_The_Old_Republic,_Threat_of_Peace "Star Wars: The Old Republic, Threat of Peace")* based on the game, also covering its backstory and introducing some characters expected in the game. The comic is released in three page spurts every other Friday.[[103]](#cite_note-103) [Satele Shan](/wiki/Satele_Shan "Satele Shan"), a character who appeared in the comics series, has been confirmed as the descendant of Bastila Shan. After three arcs were released and *Threat of Peace* was completed, a new serial entitled [*Blood of the Empire*](/wiki/Star_Wars:_The_Old_Republic,_Blood_of_the_Empire "Star Wars: The Old Republic, Blood of the Empire") began being released on the same schedule. A series of [in-universe videos](/wiki/Galactic_Timeline "Galactic Timeline") chronicling the history of the galaxy leading up to the game was also released, detailing in reverse chronological order how the political setting of the game had been in the making for thousands of years. In *[Timeline 8: The Jedi Civil War](/wiki/Timeline_8:_The_Jedi_Civil_War "Timeline 8: The Jedi Civil War")* and *[Timeline 9: The Mandalorian Wars](/wiki/Timeline_9:_The_Mandalorian_Wars "Timeline 9: The Mandalorian Wars")* covered the events behind *Star Wars; Knight of the Old Republic*, featuring what lead to the fall of Revan and Malak. These retconned the reasons that the pair set out in search of the Star Maps. They established that instead of seeking them out of their own volition, the two had met the [Sith Emperor](/wiki/Tenebrae "Tenebrae") when they journeyed into deep space following the Mandalorian Wars. It was the Emperor who turned them to the dark side and told them to find the Maps.[[104]](#cite_note-Timeline-104)

Additionally, the game spawned a series of novels, the third of which was entitled *[The Old Republic: Revan](/wiki/The_Old_Republic:_Revan "The Old Republic: Revan")*. It served as a sequel to both *Knights of the Old Republic* games and explained what happened to both Revan and the Jedi Exile, identified as Meetra Surik, after they both left for the Unknown Regions. What Revan had remembered after the events of his game was the Sith Empire and he had left to fight them. As a tie-in to *The Old Republic*, it also served as a connection between the two games and the MMORPG. The novel saw Revan placed in stasis, from which he was woken three-hundred years later as a character in *The Old Republic*. Bastila Shan also appeared in the game as a projection from the [Noetikon of Secrets](/wiki/Noetikon_of_Secrets "Noetikon of Secrets"), a holocron that contained her wisdom and personality alongside two other Jedi Masters. HK-47 had searched for his master for the full three centuries before being reunited with him and assigned to defend a Rakatan space station called the [Foundry](/wiki/Foundry_(space_station) "Foundry (space station)").

Taris returns for *The Old Republic* as a world still in ruins, the former ecumenopolis being claimed by forest growth and a rakghoul infestation. Primarily, white rakghouls like those from *Knights of the Old Republic* are encountered, though they have evolved over the centuries, but certain ones are colored red as seen in the comic series. Early on, the creative team behind *The Old Republic* wanted to include a planet from the original game and they felt Taris would be an interesting setting, allowing players to see after so long what had happened to the surface of the iconic planet. As a major planet, it was cast as a world that was very symbolic to both of *The Old Republic*'s factions, the Sith and Republic. The Republic wanted to rebuild it to show they could beat back the Sith while the Sith wanted to stop the restoration efforts to prove the Republic could not overcome them.[[15]](#cite_note-Returning_to_Taris-15)
